-# Google Calendar MCP Server
-
-This is a Model Context Protocol (MCP) server that provides integration with Google Calendar. 
-It allows LLMs application manage calendar events through a standardized interface.
-
-## Features
-
-- List available calendars
-- List events from a calendar
-- Create new calendar events
-- Update existing events
-- Delete events
-
-## Google Cloud Setup
-
-1. Go to the [Google Cloud Console](https://console.cloud.google.com)
-2. Create a new project or select an existing one.
-3. Enable the [Google Calendar API](https://console.cloud.google.com/apis/library/calendar-json.googleapis.com).
-4. Create OAuth 2.0 credentials:
-   - Go to **Credentials**
-   - Click **"Create Credentials" > "OAuth client ID"**
-   - Choose **"User data"** as the type of data the app will be accessing.
-   - Add your app name and contact information.
-   - Add the following scope (optional):
-     - `https://www.googleapis.com/auth/calendar.events`
-   - Select **"Desktop app"** as the application type.
-   - Add your email address as a test user under the [OAuth Consent screen](https://console.cloud.google.com/apis/credentials/consent).
-     - **Note:** It may take a few minutes for the test user to propagate.
-
-## Installation
-
-
-### Steps
-1. Clone the repository:
-   ```bash
-   git clone <repository-url>
-   cd gcal-mcp-server
-   ```
-2. Create a virtual environment:
-   ```bash
-   uv venv
-   # On Mac / linux
-   source .venv/bin/activate
-   # On Windows
-   .venv\Scripts\activate
-   # Install package in editable mode
-   uv pip install -e .
-   ```
-
-## Usage
-
-1. Set up the `.env` file with the required environment variables for LLMs.
-2. Run the server:
-   ```bash
-   uv run client.py
-   ```
-

In such cases, you need to \"carry over\" the excess value to the next column, making adjustments as needed. This process helps ensure that the result is accurate.\n\n**Example:**\n\nSuppose we're adding 123 and 456. Let's perform the addition step by step:\n\n1. Add the ones place (3 + 6 = 9)\n2. +      "message": "Assistant (llama3): Addition with carry over, also known as carrying or regrouping, is a fundamental concept in arithmetic that helps us perform multi-digit additions accurately.\n\nWhen adding two numbers together, we often need to add digits that are greater than 9 (e.g., 10, 11, 12, etc.). In such cases, we use the concept of carry over or regrouping to ensure that the calculation is correct.\n\nHere's a step-by-step explanation:\n\n1. **Start with the rightmost digits**: Begin by adding the rightmost digits of both numbers together (i.e., the ones place). If the result is 10 or more, you'll need to perform a carry over.\n2. **Calculate the sum without carrying**: Add the rightmost digits without considering any carry overs. Let's call this result \"X\".\n3. **Determine if there's a carry over**: Check if X is greater than or equal to 10. If it is, you'll need to perform a carry over.\n4. **Carry over**: Take the value of X and subtract 10 from it. This will give you the value that needs to be added to the next higher digit (i.e., the tens place).\n5. **Add the carried value**: Add the carried value (from step 4) to the next higher digit (tens place). Repeat this process until all digits have been processed.\n6. **Combine the results**: Combine the values from each step to get the final result.\n\nLet's use an example to illustrate this process:\n\nSuppose we want to add 456 and 278 together:\n\n1. Start with the rightmost digits: 6 (ones place) + 8 = 14\n2. Calculate the sum without carrying: 14 (X)\n3. Determine if there's a carry over: Yes, since X is greater than or equal to 10.\n4. Carry over: Take 14 and subtract 10, giving us 4.\n5. Add the carried value: Add 4 to the next higher digit (tens place): 45 + 4 = 49\n6. Combine the results: 456 + 278 = 734\n\nIn this example, we had a carry over from the ones place to the tens place. We repeated the process until all digits were processed, and then combined the results to get the final answer.\n\nAddition with carry over is an essential skill in arithmetic, as it helps you perform complex calculations accurately. With practice, you'll become more comfortable applying this concept to solve multi-digit addition problems!",

+      "timestamp": "3:45:27 PM",
+      "message": "Assistant (llama3): Addition with carry-over, also known as regrouping or borrowing, is a fundamental concept in basic arithmetic operations like addition and subtraction. It's crucial to understand how it works to perform calculations accurately.\n\n**What is carry-over?**\n\nIn basic arithmetic, we add digits from right to left (or subtract them). When you're adding numbers with multiple digits, the digits can have different values. In some cases, the sum of two digits will be greater than 9 or less than 0. That's where carry-over comes in.\n\n**How does it work?**\n\nLet's say you're adding two numbers: 123 and 456. You start by adding the rightmost (least significant) digit:\n\n1 + 6 = 7 (no carry)\n\nNext, you add the next digits:\n\n3 + 5 + 0 (carry from the previous step) = 8\n\nNow, you have a total of 8, but since it's greater than 9, you need to carry over the excess amount (1 in this case):\n\n1 + 2 + 4 + 5 = 12 (with the carried 1)\n\n**Key points:**\n\n1. When adding two digits and the result is greater than 9 or less than 0, you need to perform a carry-over.\n2. The carry-over value is added to the next most significant digit being added.\n3. If the carry-over value is 10 (or more), you'll need to perform another carry-over.\n\n**Example:**\n\nLet's add 234 and 567:\n\n1. Start with the rightmost digits: 4 + 7 = 11 (carry 1)\n2. Add the next digits: 3 + 5 + 0 (carry from step 1) = 8\n3. Carry over the excess amount (1): 1 + 2 + 6 + 5 = 14\n\n**Why is carry-over important?**\n\nCarry-over ensures that you accurately calculate the sum of two numbers, even when the digits have different values. It's a crucial concept in basic arithmetic operations and is used extensively in more complex calculations like multiplication and long division.\n\nI hope this explanation helps you understand addition with carry-over!",

In such cases, we use the concept of carry over or regrouping to ensure that the calculation is correct.\n\nHere's a step-by-step explanation:\n\n1. **Start with the rightmost digits**: Begin by adding the rightmost digits of both numbers together (i.e., the ones place). If the result is 10 or more, you'll need to perform a carry over.\n2. **Calculate the sum without carrying**: Add the rightmost digits without considering any carry overs. Let's call this result \"X\".\n3. **Determine if there's a carry over**: Check if X is greater than or equal to 10. If it is, you'll need to perform a carry over.\n4. **Carry over**: Take the value of X and subtract 10 from it. This will give you the value that needs to be added to the next higher digit (i.e., the tens place).\n5. **Add the carried value**: Add the carried value (from step 4) to the next higher digit (tens place). Repeat this process until all digits have been processed.\n6. **Combine the results**: Combine the values from each step to get the final result.\n\nLet's use an example to illustrate this process:\n\nSuppose we want to add 456 and 278 together:\n\n1. Start with the rightmost digits: 6 (ones place) + 8 = 14\n2. Calculate the sum without carrying: 14 (X)\n3. Determine if there's a carry over: Yes, since X is greater than or equal to 10.\n4. Carry over: Take 14 and subtract 10, giving us 4.\n5. Add the carried value: Add 4 to the next higher digit (tens place): 45 + 4 = 49\n6. Combine the results: 456 + 278 = 734\n\nIn this example, we had a carry over from the ones place to the tens place. We repeated the process until all digits were processed, and then combined the results to get the final answer.\n\nAddition with carry over is an essential skill in arithmetic, as it helps you perform complex calculations accurately. When you add these numbers together, you get:\n\n234 + 567 = 801\n\nBut what if I told you that the actual sum is actually 801 plus one? In such cases, we use the concept of carry over or regrouping to ensure that the calculation is correct.\n\nHere's a step-by-step explanation:\n\n1. **Start with the rightmost digits**: Begin by adding the rightmost digits of both numbers together (i.e., the ones place). If the result is 10 or more, you'll need to perform a carry over.\n2. **Calculate the sum without carrying**: Add the rightmost digits without considering any carry overs. Let's call this result \"X\".\n3. **Determine if there's a carry over**: Check if X is greater than or equal to 10. If it is, you'll need to perform a carry over.\n4. **Carry over**: Take the value of X and subtract 10 from it. This will give you the value that needs to be added to the next higher digit (i.e., the tens place).\n5. **Add the carried value**: Add the carried value (from step 4) to the next higher digit (tens place). Repeat this process until all digits have been processed.\n6. **Combine the results**: Combine the values from each step to get the final result.\n\nLet's use an example to illustrate this process:\n\nSuppose we want to add 456 and 278 together:\n\n1. Start with the rightmost digits: 6 (ones place) + 8 = 14\n2. Calculate the sum without carrying: 14 (X)\n3. Determine if there's a carry over: Yes, since X is greater than or equal to 10.\n4. Carry over: Take 14 and subtract 10, giving us 4.\n5. Add the carried value: Add 4 to the next higher digit (tens place): 45 + 4 = 49\n6. Combine the results: 456 + 278 = 734\n\nIn this example, we had a carry over from the ones place to the tens place. We repeated the process until all digits were processed, and then combined the results to get the final answer.\n\nAddition with carry over is an essential skill in arithmetic, as it helps you perform complex calculations accurately. With practice, you'll become more comfortable applying this concept to solve multi-digit addition problems!",

Start by aligning the two numbers being added, making sure that the rightmost digits are lined up.\n2. Begin by adding the rightmost digits of both numbers (the ones place). If the sum is 10 or less, simply write down the result and move to the next column.\n3. If the sum is greater than 10, you have a \"carry-over\" situation. In this case, write down the rightmost digit of the sum (the ones place), and carry over the excess amount to the next column.\n4. Repeat steps 2-3 for each subsequent column, working your way from right to left.\n5. When you reach the leftmost column (the thousands place or higher), repeat the process until all columns have been added.\n\nHere's an example:\n\nLet's say we want to add 456 and 278 together using carry-over addition.\n\nStep 1: Align the numbers\n\n```\n    456\n+   278\n```\n\nStep 2: Add the rightmost digits (ones place)\n\n```\n    456\n+   278\n    734\n```\n\nThe sum of the ones place is 6 + 8 = 14. Since 14 > 10, we have a carry-over situation.\n\nStep 3: Carry over the excess amount to the next column (tens place)\n\n```\n    456\n+   278\n  1 34\n```\n\nNow, add the digits in the tens place:\n\n```\n    4 + 7 = 11 (write down the rightmost digit and carry over the excess)\n  1 34\n```\n\nStep 4: Add the digits in the hundreds place\n\n```\n    45 + 27 = 72\n  1 34\n```\n\nAnd so on, until all columns have been added.\n\nThe final result is:\n\n```\n  734\n```\n\nBy using carry-over addition, you can add large numbers together accurately and efficiently.",

It's essential when dealing with multi-digit numbers and helps us add larger numbers correctly.\n\nHere's how it works:\n\n1. **Normal Addition**: When adding two digits, you simply add the corresponding digits together (e.g., 5 + 3 = 8).\n2. **Carry-Over**: When the sum of the added digits exceeds the maximum value for a single digit (i.e., 9), you \"carry\" the excess value to the next higher place value.\n\nLet's illustrate this with an example:\n\nSuppose we're adding 17 and 25. We start by adding the ones digits: 7 + 5 = 12. Since 12 is greater than 9, we need to carry the extra 3 (10 - 9 = 1) to the tens place.\n\nIn the tens place, we add the carried value (3) and the original tens values (17 + 20 = 37). This gives us a total of 43 in the tens place.\n\nFinally, we add the hundreds place values: 1 (from 17) + 2 (from 25) + 40 (carried from the tens place) = 43. So, our final answer is:\n\n17 + 25 = 42\n\nIn summary, when adding multi-digit numbers, you perform normal addition for each digit until you reach a value greater than 9. Then, you carry the excess value to the next higher place value and continue adding. This process ensures that your calculation is accurate and takes into account any regrouping or carrying necessary.\n\nI hope this explanation helps!",

Start by adding the rightmost (least significant) digits of the numbers being added.\n2. +      "model": "llama3"

+      "timestamp": "2025-05-09T09:56:21.045Z",
+      "type": "chat",
+      "userMessage": "Explain to me about addition with carry over."

+    {
+      "timestamp": "2025-05-09T09:56:28.040Z",
+      "type": "chat",
+      "llmResponse": "Addition with carry over, also known as carrying or regrouping, is a fundamental concept in arithmetic that helps us perform multi-digit additions accurately.\n\nWhen adding two numbers together, we often need to add digits that are greater than 9 (e.g., 10, 11, 12, etc.). In such cases, we use the concept of carry over or regrouping to ensure that the calculation is correct.\n\nHere's a step-by-step explanation:\n\n1. **Start with the rightmost digits**: Begin by adding the rightmost digits of both numbers together (i.e., the ones place). If the result is 10 or more, you'll need to perform a carry over.\n2. **Calculate the sum without carrying**: Add the rightmost digits without considering any carry overs. Let's call this result \"X\".\n3. **Determine if there's a carry over**: Check if X is greater than or equal to 10. If it is, you'll need to perform a carry over.\n4. **Carry over**: Take the value of X and subtract 10 from it. This will give you the value that needs to be added to the next higher digit (i.e., the tens place).\n5. **Add the carried value**: Add the carried value (from step 4) to the next higher digit (tens place). Repeat this process until all digits have been processed.\n6. **Combine the results**: Combine the values from each step to get the final result.\n\nLet's use an example to illustrate this process:\n\nSuppose we want to add 456 and 278 together:\n\n1. Start with the rightmost digits: 6 (ones place) + 8 = 14\n2. Calculate the sum without carrying: 14 (X)\n3. Determine if there's a carry over: Yes, since X is greater than or equal to 10.\n4. Carry over: Take 14 and subtract 10, giving us 4.\n5. Add the carried value: Add 4 to the next higher digit (tens place): 45 + 4 = 49\n6. Combine the results: 456 + 278 = 734\n\nIn this example, we had a carry over from the ones place to the tens place. We repeated the process until all digits were processed, and then combined the results to get the final answer.\n\nAddition with carry over is an essential skill in arithmetic, as it helps you perform complex calculations accurately. With practice, you'll become more comfortable applying this concept to solve multi-digit addition problems!",

When you're adding numbers with multiple digits, the digits can have different values. In some cases, the sum of two digits will be greater than 9 or less than 0. That's where carry-over comes in.\n\n**How does it work?**\n\nLet's say you're adding two numbers: 123 and 456. Add the next digits: 3 + 5 + 0 (carry from step 1) = 8\n3. Continue this process until all digits have been added and any carries have been propagated.\n\nFor example, let's say we want to add 456 and 278:\n\n```\n    456\n+   278\n------\n    734\n```\n\nTo start, we add the ones place values (6 + 8 = 14):\n\n```\n    456\n+   278\n--------\n     4(14)\n```\n\nSince 14 is greater than 10, we carry a 1 to the tens column and write down the 4:\n\n```\n    456\n+   278\n--------\n    1 4\n```\n\nNext, we add the tens place values (50 + 70 = 120):\n\n```\n    456\n+   278\n--------\n    14\n```\n\nWe still need to carry a 1 from this sum:\n\n```\n    456\n+   278\n--------\n    11 4\n```\n\nFinally, we add the hundreds place values (400 + 200 = 600):\n\n```\n    456\n+   278\n--------\n  6 14\n```\n\nAnd that's it! diff --git a/src/components/panels/QRCodeGenerator.jsx b/src/components/panels/QRCodeGenerator.jsx
new file mode 100644
index 0000000..b311693
--- /dev/null
+++ b/src/components/panels/QRCodeGenerator.jsx
@@ -0,0 +1,34 @@
+import React, { useState } from 'react';
+import { QRCodeSVG } from 'qrcode.react';
+
+const QRCodeGenerator = () => {
+    const [url, setUrl] = useState('');
+
+    return (
+        <div className="flex flex-col items-center gap-6">
+            <div className="w-full">
+                <label 
+                    htmlFor="qr-input" 
+                    className="block text-sm font-medium text-gray-700 mb-2"
+                >
+                    Enter URL or text to generate QR code
+                </label>
+                <input
+                    id="qr-input"
+                    type="text"
+                    value={url}
+                    onChange={(e) => setUrl(e.target.value)}
+                    placeholder="https://example.com"
+                    className="w-full px-4 py-3 border border-gray-300 rounded-lg shadow-sm focus:outline-none focus:ring-2 focus:ring-blue-500 focus:border-blue-500"
+                />
+            </div>
+            {url && (
+                <div className="p-6 bg-white rounded-lg shadow-md border border-gray-200">
+                    <QRCodeSVG value={url} size={256} />
+                </div>
+            )}
+        </div>
+    );
+};
+
+export default QRCodeGenerator;

+  // Add this function after other function declarations
+  // Update the processNaturalLanguageCommand function
+  const processNaturalLanguageCommand = (text) => {
+    // Helper function to calculate similarity between two strings
+    const calculateSimilarity = (str1, str2) => {
+      const s1 = str1.toLowerCase();
+      const s2 = str2.toLowerCase();
+      const len1 = s1.length;
+      const len2 = s2.length;
+      const matrix = Array(len1 + 1).fill().map(() => Array(len2 + 1).fill(0));
+
+      for (let i = 0; i <= len1; i++) matrix[i][0] = i;
+      for (let j = 0; j <= len2; j++) matrix[0][j] = j;
+
+      for (let i = 1; i <= len1; i++) {
+        for (let j = 1; j <= len2; j++) {
+          const cost = s1[i - 1] === s2[j - 1] ? 0 : 1;
+          matrix[i][j] = Math.min(
+            matrix[i - 1][j] + 1,
+            matrix[i][j - 1] + 1,
+            matrix[i - 1][j - 1] + cost
+          );
+        }
+      }
+      return 1 - (matrix[len1][len2] / Math.max(len1, len2));
+    };
+
+    // Find closest matching command
+    const findClosestCommand = (input) => {
+      const commands = Object.keys(commandMap);
+      let bestMatch = null;
+      let highestSimilarity = 0;
+
+      commands.forEach(cmd => {
+        const similarity = calculateSimilarity(input, cmd);
+        if (similarity > highestSimilarity && similarity > 0.6) { // Threshold of 60% similarity
+          highestSimilarity = similarity;
+          bestMatch = cmd;
+        }
+      });
+      return bestMatch;
+    };
+
+    const commandMap = {
+      'read': 'cat',
+      'show': 'cat',
+      'list': 'ls',
+      'show files': 'ls',
+      'show directory': 'ls',
+      'current directory': 'pwd',
+      'where am i': 'pwd',
+      'clear screen': 'clear',
+      'make directory': 'mkdir',
+      'create directory': 'mkdir',
+      'remove': 'rm',
+      'delete': 'rm',
+    };
+
+    // Fuzzy patterns for file operations
+    const patterns = {
+      read: /(?:r[ea]+d|sh[o0]w|d[i1]spl[ae]y|[o0]p[e3]n)\s+(?:c[o0]nt[e3]nts?\s+[o0]f\s+|th[e3]\s+)?(?:f[i1]l[e3]\s+)?["']?([^"']+?)["']?\s*$/i,
+      list: /(?:l[i1]st|sh[o0]w)\s+(?:f[i1]l[e3]s?|d[i1]r[e3]ct[o0]r[yi]?s?|c[o0]nt[e3]nts?)\s*(?:[i1]n\s+)?(.+)?/i,
+      mkdir: /(?:m[a4]k[e3]|cr[e3][a4]t[e3])\s+(?:[a4]\s+)?(?:n[e3]w\s+)?d[i1]r(?:[e3]ct[o0]r[yi])?\s+(?:n[a4]m[e3]d\s+)?(.+)/i,
+      remove: /(?:r[e3]m[o0]v[e3]|d[e3]l[e3]t[e3])\s+(?:th[e3]\s+)?(?:f[i1]l[e3]|d[i1]r[e3]ct[o0]r[yi])?\s+(.+)/i,
+      where: /w[he]{1,2}r[e]?\s+(?:am|is)\s+(?:i|me|we)/i
+    };
+
+    let command = '';
+    const input = text.toLowerCase().trim();
+
+    // First try to find exact match
+    if (commandMap[input]) {
+      return commandMap[input];
+    }
+
+    // Then try to find closest match for simple commands
+    const closestMatch = findClosestCommand(input);
+    if (closestMatch) {
+      return commandMap[closestMatch];
+    }
+
+    // Check patterns with fuzzy matching
+    if (patterns.where.test(input)) {
+      command = 'pwd';
+    } else if (patterns.read.test(input)) {
+      const match = input.match(patterns.read);
+      const filename = match[1].trim();
+      command = `cat "${filename}"`;

+      const match = input.match(patterns.list);
+      command = `ls ${match[1] ? `"${match[1].trim()}"` : ''}`.trim();
+    } else if (patterns.mkdir.test(input)) {
+      const match = input.match(patterns.mkdir);
+      command = `mkdir "${match[1].trim()}"`;
+    } else if (patterns.remove.test(input)) {
+      const match = input.match(patterns.remove);
+      command = `rm "${match[1].trim()}"`;
+    }
+
+    return command;
+  };

+      const timestamp = new Date().toISOString();
+      const hash = await generateHash(screenshot);
+      const g_time = `sha256|${timestamp}|ASIA`;
+      
+      // Create a File object from the screenshot buffer
+      const file = new Blob([screenshot], { type: 'image/png' });
+      
+      // Create form data for upload
+      const formData = new FormData();
+      formData.append('file', file, `${name}.png`);
+      
+      const metadata = {
+        fileName: `${name}.png`,
+        mimeType: 'image/png',
+        size: screenshot.length,
+        description: `Playwright automated test screenshot: ${name}`,
+        timestamp: timestamp,
+        source: 'playwright_automation'
+      };
+      
+      formData.append('metadata', JSON.stringify(metadata));
+      formData.append('action', 'add');
+      
+      // Upload using the catalog API
+      const response = await fetch('http://localhost:4321/api/card-collection?action=add', {
+        method: 'POST',
+        body: formData
+      });
+  
+      if (!response.ok) {
+        throw new Error(`Failed to upload screenshot: ${response.statusText}`);
+      }
+  
+      const result = await response.json();
+      return result.hash;
+    } catch (error) {
+      console.error(`Error saving screenshot ${name}:`, error);
+      throw error;
+    }
+  }

+
+// Helper function to generate hash for screenshots
+async function generateHash(buffer) {
+  const msgUint8 = new TextEncoder().encode(buffer.toString('base64'));
+  const hashBuffer = await crypto.subtle.digest('SHA-256', msgUint8);
+  const hashArray = Array.from(new Uint8Array(hashBuffer));
+  const hashHex = hashArray.map(b => b.toString(16).padStart(2, '0')).join('');
+  return hashHex;
+}
